<p>The <b>Most Excellent Order of the British Empire</b> is a British <a href="/wiki/Order_of_chivalry" title="Order of chivalry">order of chivalry</a>, rewarding contributions to the arts and sciences, work with charitable and welfare organisations, and public service outside the <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">Civil service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obe_royal_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-obe_royal-2">[2]</a></sup> It was established on 4 June 1917 by <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">King George V</a>, and comprises five classes across both civil and military divisions, the most senior two of which make the recipient either a <a href="/wiki/Orders,_decorations,_and_medals_of_the_United_Kingdom#Modern_honours" title="Orders, decorations, and medals of the United Kingdom">knight</a> if male or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dame_(title)" title="Dame (title)">dame</a> if female.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> There is also the related <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Medal" title="British Empire Medal">British Empire Medal</a>, whose recipients are affiliated with, but not members of, the order.</p>
<p>Recommendations for appointments to the Order of the British Empire were at first made on the nomination of the United Kingdom, the self-governing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominions" title="Dominions">Dominions</a> of the Empire (later Commonwealth) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_India" title="Viceroy of India">Viceroy of India</a>. Nominations continue today from Commonwealth countries that participate in recommending British (Imperial) honours. Most Commonwealth countries, such as India, Pakistan, and Nigeria, ceased recommendations for appointments to the Order of the British Empire when they created their own honours. Some countries, such as Canada and Australia, were still recommending appointments to the Order months or years after the creation of their own national orders of chivalry.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_classes">Current classes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Current classes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The five classes of appointment to the Order are, in descending order of precedence:</p>
<ol>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Grand_Cross" title="Grand Cross">Knight Grand Cross</a></b> or <b>Dame Grand Cross</b> of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire (<b>GBE</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[a]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Commander_(order)" title="Commander (order)">Knight Commander</a></b> or <b><a href="/wiki/List_of_Dames_Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="List of Dames Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Dame Commander</a></b> of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire (<b>KBE</b> or <b>DBE</b>)</li>
<li><b>Commander</b> of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire (<b>CBE</b>)</li>
<li><b>Officer</b> of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire (<b>OBE</b>)</li>
<li><b>Member</b> of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire (<b>MBE</b>)</li>
</ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Styles_and_honorary_knighthoods">Styles and honorary knighthoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Styles and honorary knighthoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The senior two ranks of Knight or Dame Grand Cross, and Knight or Dame Commander, entitle their members to use the title of <i>Sir</i> for men and <i>Dame</i> for women before their forename. Most members are citizens of the United Kingdom or the Commonwealth realms that use the Imperial system of honours and awards.</p>
<p>Honorary knighthoods are appointed to citizens of nations where <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">the Queen</a> is not <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, and may permit use of post-nominal letters but not the title of <i>Sir</i> or <i>Dame</i>. Occasionally, honorary appointees are, incorrectly, referred to as Sir or Dame – <a href="/wiki/Bob_Geldof" title="Bob Geldof">Bob Geldof</a>, for example. Honorary appointees who later become a citizen of a Commonwealth realm can convert their appointment from honorary to substantive, then enjoy all privileges of membership of the order, including use of the title of <i>Sir</i> and <i>Dame</i> for the senior two ranks of the Order. An example is Irish broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Terry_Wogan" title="Terry Wogan">Terry Wogan</a>, who was appointed an honorary Knight Commander of the Order in 2005, and on successful application for British citizenship, held alongside his Irish citizenship, was made a substantive member and subsequently styled as Sir Terry Wogan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">King George V</a> founded the Order to fill gaps in the <a href="/wiki/Orders,_decorations,_and_medals_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Orders, decorations, and medals of the United Kingdom">British honours system</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter" title="Order of the Garter">Most Noble Order of the Garter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Thistle" title="Order of the Thistle">Most Ancient and Most Noble Order of the Thistle</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St_Patrick" title="Order of St Patrick">Most Illustrious Order of Saint Patrick</a> honoured members of royal families, peers, statesmen, and eminent military commanders;</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Bath" title="Order of the Bath">Most Honourable Order of the Bath</a> honoured senior military officers and civil servants;</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St_Michael_and_St_George" title="Order of St Michael and St George">Most Distinguished Order of St Michael and St George</a> honoured diplomats and colonial officials;</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Star_of_India" title="Order of the Star of India">Most Exalted Order of the Star of India</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Indian_Empire" title="Order of the Indian Empire">Most Eminent Order of the Indian Empire</a> honoured Indian rulers and British and Indian officials of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Indian_Empire" title="British Indian Empire">British Indian Empire</a>; and</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victorian_Order" title="Royal Victorian Order">Royal Victorian Order</a>, in the personal gift of the monarch, honoured those who had personally served the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Royal_Family" title="British Royal Family">Royal Family</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>In particular, King George V wished to create an Order to honour many thousands of those who had served in a variety of non-combatant roles during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>. When first established, the Order had only one division. However, in 1918, soon after its foundation, it was formally divided into Military and <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">Civil</a> Divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> The Order's motto is <i>For God and the Empire</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obe_royal_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-obe_royal-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the foundation of the Order, the 'Medal of the Order of the British Empire' was instituted, to serve as a lower award granting recipients affiliation but not membership. In 1922, this was renamed the '<a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Medal" title="British Empire Medal">British Empire Medal</a>' (BEM). It stopped being awarded by the United Kingdom as part of the <a href="/wiki/Orders,_decorations,_and_medals_of_the_United_Kingdom#Reform" title="Orders, decorations, and medals of the United Kingdom">1993 reforms</a> to the honours system, but was again awarded beginning in 2012, starting with 293 BEMs awarded for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diamond_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Diamond Jubilee of Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II's Diamond Jubilee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> In addition, the BEM is awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> and by some other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> nations. In 2004, a report entitled "A Matter of Honour: Reforming Our Honours System" by a <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">Commons</a> committee recommended to phase out the Order of the British Empire, as its title was "now considered to be unacceptable, being thought to embody values that are no longer shared by many of the country's population".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">British monarch</a> is Sovereign of the Order, and appoints all other members of the Order (by convention, on the advice of the governments of the United Kingdom and some <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>). The next most senior member is the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Master_(order)" title="Grand Master (order)">Grand Master</a>, of whom there have been three: <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII" title="Edward VIII">Prince Edward, the Prince of Wales</a> (1917–1936); <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Teck" title="Mary of Teck">Queen Mary</a> (1936–1953); and the current Grand Master, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">the Duke of Edinburgh</a> (since 1953).</p>
<p>The Order is limited to 300 Knights and Dames Grand Cross, 845 Knights and Dames Commander, and 8,960 Commanders. There are no limits applied to the total number of members of the fourth and fifth classes, but no more than 858 Officers and 1,464 Members may be appointed per year. Foreign appointees, as honorary members, do not contribute to the numbers restricted to the Order as full members do. Although the Order of the British Empire has by far the highest number of members of the British Orders of Chivalry, with over 100,000 living members worldwide, there are fewer appointments to knighthoods than in other orders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obe_royal_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-obe_royal-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Though men can be <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighted separately from an order of chivalry</a>, women cannot, and so the rank of Knight/Dame Commander of the Order is the lowest rank of damehood, and second-lowest of knighthood (above Knights Bachelor). Because of this, an appointment as Dame Commander is made in circumstances in which a man would be created a Knight Bachelor. For example, by convention, female judges of the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court of Justice</a> are created Dames Commander after appointment, while male judges become Knights Bachelor.</p>
<p>The Order has six officials: the Prelate; the Dean; the Secretary; the Registrar; the King of Arms; and the Usher. The <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_London" title="Bishop of London">Bishop of London</a>, a senior bishop in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>, serves as the Order's Prelate. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Deans_of_St_Paul%27s" title="List of Deans of St Paul's">Dean of St Paul's</a> is <i><a href="/wiki/Ex_officio_member" title="Ex officio member">ex officio</a></i> the Dean of the Order. The <a href="/wiki/King_of_Arms_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="King of Arms of the Order of the British Empire">Order's King of Arms</a> is not a member of the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Arms" title="College of Arms">College of Arms</a>, as are many other <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">heraldic</a> officers. The Usher of the Order is known as the <a href="/wiki/Gentleman_Usher_of_the_Purple_Rod" title="Gentleman Usher of the Purple Rod">Gentleman Usher of the Purple Rod</a>; he does not – unlike his <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter" title="Order of the Garter">Order of the Garter</a> equivalent, the <a href="/wiki/Black_Rod" title="Black Rod">Gentleman Usher of the Black Rod</a> – perform any duties related to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>.</p>
<p>From time to time, individuals are appointed to a higher grade within the Order, thereby ceasing usage of the junior post-nominal letters.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallantry">Gallantry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Gallantry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>From 1940, the Sovereign could appoint a person as a Commander, Officer or Member of the Order of the British Empire for gallantry for acts of bravery (not in the face of the enemy) below the level required for the <a href="/wiki/George_Medal" title="George Medal">George Medal</a>. The grade was determined by the same criteria as usual, and not by the level of gallantry (and with more junior people instead receiving the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Medal" title="British Empire Medal">British Empire Medal</a>). Oddly, this meant that it was awarded for lesser acts of gallantry than the George Medal, but, as an Order, was worn before it and listed before it in post-nominal initials. From 14 January 1958, these awards were designated the Order of the British Empire for Gallantry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Any individual made a member of the Order for gallantry could wear an emblem of two crossed silver oak leaves on the same riband, ribbon or bow as the badge. It could not be awarded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Posthumous_award" title="Posthumous award">posthumously</a>, and was effectively replaced in 1974 with the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Gallantry_Medal" title="Queen's Gallantry Medal">Queen's Gallantry Medal</a> (QGM). If recipients of the Order of the British Empire for Gallantry received promotion within the Order, whether for gallantry or otherwise, they continued to wear also the insignia of the lower grade with the oak leaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> However, they only used the post-nominal letters of the higher grade.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vestments_and_accoutrements">Vestments and accoutrements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Vestments and accoutrements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Members of the Order wear elaborate vestments on important occasions (such as quadrennial services and <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_British_monarch" title="Coronation of the British monarch">coronations</a>), which vary by rank (the designs underwent major changes in 1937):</p>
<ul>
<li>The <i>mantle</i>, worn by only Knights and Dames Grand Cross, was originally made of yellow satin lined with blue silk, but is now made of rose pink satin lined with pearl-grey silk. On the left side is a representation of the star (see below).</li>
<li>The <i>collar</i>, also worn by only Knights and Dames Grand Cross, is made of gold. It consists of six medallions depicting the Royal Arms, alternating with six medallions depicting the Royal and Imperial Cypher of George V (<i>GRI</i>, which stands for "<i><span lang="la" xml:lang="la">Georgius Rex Imperator</span></i>"). The medallions are linked with gold cables depicting lions and crowns.</li>
</ul>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerycaption">Knight/Dame Grand Cross insignia</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 285px">

</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Order_of_the_British_Empire_Insignia.jpg"><img alt="Order of the British Empire Insignia.jpg" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1705" data-file-width="605" height="620" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Order_of_the_British_Empire_Insignia.jpg/220px-Order_of_the_British_Empire_Insignia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Order_of_the_British_Empire_Insignia.jpg/330px-Order_of_the_British_Empire_Insignia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Order_of_the_British_Empire_Insignia.jpg/440px-Order_of_the_British_Empire_Insignia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Order_of_the_British_Empire_Insignia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On certain "<a href="/wiki/Collar_day" title="Collar day">collar days</a>" designated by the Sovereign, members attending formal events may wear the Order's collar over their military uniform, formal day dress, or evening wear. When collars are worn (either on collar days or on formal occasions such as coronations), the badge is suspended from the collar. Collars are returned upon the death of their owners, but other insignia may be retained.</p>
<p>At less important occasions, simpler insignia are used:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <i>star</i> is an eight-pointed silver star used by only Knights and Dames Grand Cross and Knights and Dames Commander. It is worn pinned to the left breast. Varying in size depending on class, it bears a crimson ring with the motto of the Order inscribed. Within the ring, a figure of <a href="/wiki/Britannia" title="Britannia">Britannia</a> was originally shown. Since 1937, however, the effigies of George V and Mary of Teck have been shown instead.</li>
<li>The <i>badge</i> is the only insignia used by all members of the Order. Until 1937, it was suspended on a purple ribbon, with a red central stripe for the military division; since then, the ribbon has been rose-pink with pearl-grey edges, with the addition of a pearl-grey central stripe for the military division. Knights and Dames Grand Cross wear it on a riband or sash, passing from the right shoulder to the left hip. Knights Commander and male Commanders wear the badge from a ribbon around the neck; male Officers and Members wear the badge from a ribbon on the left chest; all females other than Dames Grand Cross wear it from a bow on the left shoulder. The badge is in the form of a <i>cross <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/patonce" title="wikt:patonce">patonce</a></i> (having the arms growing broader and floriated toward the end), the obverse of which bears the same field as the star (that is, either Britannia or <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Teck" title="Mary of Teck">Queen Mary</a>); the reverse bears George V's Royal and Imperial Cypher. Both are within a ring bearing the motto of the Order. The size of the badges varies according to rank: the higher classes have slightly larger badges. The badges of Knights and Dames Grand Cross, Knights and Dames Commander and Commanders are enamelled with pale blue crosses and crimson rings; those of Officers are plain gold; those of Members are plain silver.</li>
<li>The <i>British Empire Medal</i> is made of silver. On the obverse is an image of Britannia surrounded by the motto, with the words "For Meritorious Service" at the bottom; on the reverse is George V's Imperial and Royal Cypher, with the words "Instituted by King George V" at the bottom. The name of the recipient is engraved on the rim. This medal is nicknamed 'the Gong', and comes in both a full-sized and miniature versions – the latter for formal white-tie and informal black-tie occasions.</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Award_pin" title="Award pin">lapel pin</a> for everyday wear was first announced at the end of December 2006, and is available to recipients of all levels of the Order, as well as to holders of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Medal" title="British Empire Medal">British Empire Medal</a>. The pin design is not unique to any level. The pin features the badge of the Order, enclosed in a circle of ribbon of its colours of pink and grey. Lapel pins must be purchased separately by a member of the Order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> The creation of such a pin was recommended in Sir Hayden Phillips' review of the honours system in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chapel">Chapel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Chapel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St-Pauls-Cathedral_London_Crypta_Chapel-Order-Of-The-British-Empire-01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/St-Pauls-Cathedral_London_Crypta_Chapel-Order-Of-The-British-Empire-01.jpg/220px-St-Pauls-Cathedral_London_Crypta_Chapel-Order-Of-The-British-Empire-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/St-Pauls-Cathedral_London_Crypta_Chapel-Order-Of-The-British-Empire-01.jpg/330px-St-Pauls-Cathedral_London_Crypta_Chapel-Order-Of-The-British-Empire-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/St-Pauls-Cathedral_London_Crypta_Chapel-Order-Of-The-British-Empire-01.jpg/440px-St-Pauls-Cathedral_London_Crypta_Chapel-Order-Of-The-British-Empire-01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St-Pauls-Cathedral_London_Crypta_Chapel-Order-Of-The-British-Empire-01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chapel of the Order in the crypt of <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul's Cathedral">St Paul's Cathedral</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The chapel of the Order is in the far eastern end of the crypt of <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul's Cathedral">St Paul's Cathedral</a>, but it holds its great services upstairs in the main body of the Cathedral. (The Cathedral also serves as the home of the chapel of <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St_Michael_and_St_George" title="Order of St Michael and St George">The Most Distinguished Order of St Michael and St George</a>.) Religious services for the whole Order are held every four years; new Knights and Dames Grand Cross are installed at these services. The chapel was dedicated in 1960.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Precedence_and_privileges">Precedence and privileges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Precedence and privileges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Order_of_the_British_Empire_-_Non_Arms.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1124" data-file-width="860" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Order_of_the_British_Empire_-_Non_Arms.svg/150px-Order_of_the_British_Empire_-_Non_Arms.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Order_of_the_British_Empire_-_Non_Arms.svg/225px-Order_of_the_British_Empire_-_Non_Arms.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Order_of_the_British_Empire_-_Non_Arms.svg/300px-Order_of_the_British_Empire_-_Non_Arms.svg.png 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Order_of_the_British_Empire_-_Non_Arms.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Knights, Dames and Commanders may display the <a href="/wiki/Circlet" title="Circlet">circlet</a> of the Order on the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a>, with the badge of the Order suspended from it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[b]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Knights Grand Cross and Knights Commander prefix <i>Sir</i>, and Dames Grand Cross and Dames Commander prefix <i>Dame</i>, to their forenames.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[c]</a></sup> Wives of Knights may prefix <i>Lady</i> to their surnames, but no equivalent privilege exists for husbands of Knights or spouses of Dames. Such forms are not used by peers and princes, except when the names of the former are written out in their fullest forms. Clergy of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> do not use the title <i>Sir</i> or <i>Dame</i> as they do not receive the <a href="/wiki/Accolade" title="Accolade">accolade</a> (i.e., they are not dubbed "knight" with a sword), although they do append the <a href="/wiki/Post-nominal_letters" title="Post-nominal letters">post-nominal letters</a>.</p>
<p>Knights and Dames Grand Cross use the post-nominal, <i>GBE</i>; Knights Commander, <i>KBE</i>; Dames Commander, <i>DBE</i>; Commanders, <i>CBE</i>; Officers, <i>OBE</i>; and Members, <i>MBE</i>. The post-nominal for the British Empire Medal is <i>BEM</i>.</p>
<p>Members of all classes of the Order are assigned positions in the <a href="/wiki/Orders_of_precedence_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Orders of precedence in the United Kingdom">order of precedence</a>. Wives of male members of all classes also feature on the order of precedence, as do sons, daughters and daughters-in-law of Knights Grand Cross and Knights Commander; relatives of Ladies of the Order, however, are not assigned any special precedence. As a general rule, individuals can derive precedence from their fathers or husbands, but not from their mothers or wives (see <a href="/wiki/Order_of_precedence_in_England_and_Wales" title="Order of precedence in England and Wales">order of precedence in England and Wales</a> for the exact positions).</p>
<p>Knights and Dames Grand Cross are also entitled to be granted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supporters_(heraldry)" title="Supporters (heraldry)">heraldic supporters</a>. They may, furthermore, encircle their arms with a depiction of the <a href="/wiki/Circlet" title="Circlet">circlet</a> (a circle bearing the motto) and the collar; the former is shown either outside or on top of the latter. Knights and Dames Commander and Commanders may display the circlet, but not the collar, surrounding their arms. The badge is depicted suspended from the collar or circlet.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_Knights_and_Dames_Grand_Cross">Current Knights and Dames Grand Cross</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Current Knights and Dames Grand Cross">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><b>Sovereign</b>: <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a></li>

<li><b><a href="/wiki/King_of_Arms_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="King of Arms of the Order of the British Empire">King of Arms</a></b>: Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fulton_(Royal_Marines_officer)" title="Robert Fulton (Royal Marines officer)">Sir Robert Fulton</a>, KBE</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recommendations_by_Commonwealth_countries">Recommendations by Commonwealth countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Recommendations by Commonwealth countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Recommendations for appointments to the Order of the British Empire continue to be made by some <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>. In 2016, Antigua and Barbuda, Bahamas, Barbados, Belize, Grenada, Papua New Guinea, Saint Christopher and Nevis, Saint Lucia, Solomon Islands, and Tuvalu all included Order of the British Empire awards in their New Year and/or Queen's Birthday honours lists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup> Since the Second World War, most Commonwealth realms have established their own national system of honours and awards and have created their own unique orders, decorations and medals. Canada seldom made recommendations for appointments to the Order of the British Empire except for the Second World War and Korea but continued to recommend gallantry awards for both military and civilians until after the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Canada" title="Order of Canada">Order of Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup> Australia continued to recommend the Order of the British Empire until the 1989 Queen's Birthday Honours, nearly 15 years after the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Australia" title="Order of Australia">Order of Australia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_who_have_declined_a_British_honour" title="List of people who have declined a British honour">List of people who have declined a British honour</a></div>
<p>The Order has attracted some criticism for its naming having connection with the idea of the now-extinct <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FifthReport_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FifthReport-20">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Zephaniah" title="Benjamin Zephaniah">Benjamin Zephaniah</a>, a <a href="/wiki/British_Jamaican" title="British Jamaican">British Jamaican</a> poet, publicly rejected appointment as an Officer in 2003 because, he asserted, it reminded him of "thousands of years of brutality". He also said that "It reminds me of how my foremothers were raped and my forefathers brutalised".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2004, a <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Select_committee_(Westminster_system)" title="Select committee (Westminster system)">Select Committee</a> recommended changing the name of the award to the <i>Order of British Excellence</i>, and changing the rank of <i>Commander</i> to <i>Companion</i>; as the former was said to have a "militaristic ring".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FifthReport_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-FifthReport-20">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>A notable person to decline the offer of membership was the author <a href="/wiki/C._S._Lewis" title="C. S. Lewis">C. S. Lewis</a> (1898–1963), who had been named on the last list of honours by <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a> in December 1951. Despite being a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monarchist" title="Monarchist">monarchist</a>, he declined so as to avoid association with any political issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Letters_of_C.S._Lewis_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Letters_of_C.S._Lewis-24">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The members of <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> were appointed as Members in 1965. <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a> justified the comparative merits of his investiture by comparing military membership in the Order: "Lots of people who complained about us receiving the MBE [status] received theirs for heroism in the war – for killing people ... We received ours for entertaining other people. I'd say we deserve ours more". Lennon later returned his MBE insignia on 25 November 1969, as part of his ongoing peace protests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> Other criticism centres on the claim that many recipients of the Order are being rewarded with honours for simply doing their jobs; critics claim that the Civil Service and Judiciary receive far more orders and honours than leaders of other professions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FifthReport_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-FifthReport-20">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chin_Peng" title="Chin Peng">Chin Peng</a>, long-time leader of the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Communist_Party" title="Malayan Communist Party">Malayan Communist Party</a>, was appointed as an Officer for his share in fighting against the Japanese during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, in close co-operation with the British commando <a href="/wiki/Force_136#Malayan_Communist_Party" title="Force 136">Force 136</a>. His membership was withdrawn by the British government (and became undesirable for Chin Peng himself) when the Communist leader headed his party's guerrilla insurgency against the British in the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Emergency" title="Malayan Emergency">Malayan Emergency</a> after the War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_the_British_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is common, but incorrect,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> to omit "of the Most Excellent Order" and other important words not implied by the initials.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Never surnames – thus Sir <a href="/wiki/Antony_Sher" title="Antony Sher">Antony Sher</a> may be shortened to Sir Antony, but not to Sir Sher</span></li>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="width:1%;font-weight:normal;">In the face<br/>
of the enemy</th>

<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">

<li><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Cross_(UK)_ribbon.png"><img alt="Victoria Cross (UK) ribbon.png" data-file-height="30" data-file-width="100" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Victoria_Cross_%28UK%29_ribbon.png/35px-Victoria_Cross_%28UK%29_ribbon.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Victoria_Cross_%28UK%29_ribbon.png/53px-Victoria_Cross_%28UK%29_ribbon.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Victoria_Cross_%28UK%29_ribbon.png/70px-Victoria_Cross_%28UK%29_ribbon.png 2x" width="35"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Cross" title="Victoria Cross">Victoria Cross</a> (VC)</span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dso-ribbon.png"><img alt="Dso-ribbon.png" data-file-height="30" data-file-width="100" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Dso-ribbon.png/35px-Dso-ribbon.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Dso-ribbon.png/53px-Dso-ribbon.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Dso-ribbon.png/70px-Dso-ribbon.png 2x" width="35"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Order" title="Distinguished Service Order">Distinguished Service Order</a> (DSO)</span></li>
